6z\"></path></svg></a>Installation</h2>\n<p><code>npm install cheerio</code></p>\n<h2><a id=\"user-content-features\" class=\"deep-link\" href=\"#features\" aria-hidden=\"true\" rel=\"nofollow\"><svg aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"deep-link-icon\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewbox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"><path d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path></svg></a>Features</h2>\n<p><strong>❤ Familiar syntax:</strong>\nCheerio implements a subset of core jQuery. Cheerio removes all the DOM inconsistencies and browser cruft from the jQuery library, revealing its truly gorgeous API.</p>\n<p><strong>ϟ Blazingly fast:</strong>\nCheerio works with a very simple, consistent DOM model. As a result parsing, manipulating, and rendering are incredibly efficient. Preliminary end-to-end benchmarks suggest that cheerio is about <strong>8x</strong> faster than JSDOM.</p>\n<p><strong>❁ Incredibly flexible:</strong>\nCheerio wraps around <a href=\"https://github.com/inikulin/parse5\" rel=\"nofollow\">parse5</a> parser and can optionally use @FB55's forgiving <a href=\"https://github.com/fb55/htmlparser2/\" rel=\"nofollow\">htmlparser2</a>. Cheerio can parse nearly any HTML or XML document.</p>\n<h2><a id=\"user-content-cheerio-is-not-a-web-browser\" class=\"deep-link\" href=\"#cheerio-is-not-a-web-browser\" aria-hidden=\"true\" rel=\"nofollow\"><svg aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"deep-link-icon\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewbox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"><path d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path></svg></a>Cheerio is not a web browser</h2>\n<p>Cheerio parses markup and provides an API for traversing/manipulating the resulting data structure. It does not interpret the result as a web browser does. Specifically, it does <em>not</em> produce a visual rendering, apply CSS, load external resources, or execute JavaScript. If your use case requires any of this functionality, you should consider projects like <a href=\"http://phantomjs.org/\" rel=\"nofollow\">PhantomJS</a> or <a href=\"https://github.com/tmpvar/jsdom\" rel=\"nofollow\">JSDom</a>.</p>\n<h2><a id=\"user-content-job-board\" class=\"deep-link\" href=\"#job-board\" aria-hidden=\"true\" rel=\"nofollow\"><svg aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"deep-link-icon\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewbox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"><path d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path></svg></a>Job Board</h2>\n<p>Looking for a career upgrade? The default options are:</p>\n<div class=\"highlight js\"><pre class=\"editor editor-colors\"><div class=\"line\"><span class=\"source js\"><span class=\"meta brace curly js\"><span>{</span></span></span></div><div class=\"line\"><span class=\"source js\"><span>    withDomLvl1</span><span class=\"keyword operator assignment js\"><span>:</span></span><span> </span><span class=\"constant language boolean true js\"><span>true</span></span><span class=\"meta delimiter object comma js\"><span>,</span></span></span></div><div class=\"line\"><span class=\"source js\"><span>    normalizeWhitespace</span><span class=\"keyword operator assignment js\"><span>:</span></span><span> </span><span class=\"constant language boolean false js\"><span>false</span></span><span class=\"meta delimiter object comma js\"><span>,</span></span></span></div><div class=\"line\"><span class=\"source js\"><span>    xmlMode</span><span class=\"keyword operator assignment js\"><span>:</span></span><span> </span><span class=\"constant language boolean true js\"><span>true</span></span><span class=\"meta delimiter object comma js\"><span>,</span></span></span></div><div class=\"line\"><span class=\"source js\"><span>    decodeEntities</span><span class=\"keyword operator assignment js\"><span>:</span></span><span> </span><span class=\"constant language boolean true js\"><span>true</span></span></span></div><div class=\"line\"><span class=\"source js\"><span class=\"meta brace curly js\"><span>}</span></span></span></div></pre></div>\n<p>For a full list of options and their effects, see <a href=\"https://github.com/fb55/DomHandler\" rel=\"nofollow\">this</a> and\n<a href=\"https://github.com/fb55/htmlparser2/wiki/Parser-options\" rel=\"nofollow\">htmlparser2's options</a>.</p>\n<p>Some users may wish to parse markup with the <code>htmlparser2</code> library, and\ntraverse/manipulate the resulting structure with Cheerio. This may be the case\nfor those upgrading from pre-1.0 releases of Cheerio (which relied on\n<code>htmlparser2</code>), for those dealing with invalid markup (because <code>htmlparser2</code> is\nmore forgiving), or for those operating in performance-critical situations\n(because <code>htmlparser2</code> may be faster in some cases). Note that &quot;more forgiving&quot;\nmeans <code>htmlparser2</code> has error-correcting mechanisms that aren't always a match\nfor the standards observed by web browsers. This behavior may be useful when\nparsing non-HTML content.</p>\n<p>To support these cases, <code>load</code> also accepts a <code>htmlparser2</code>-compatible data\nstructure as its first argument. Users may install <code>htmlparser2</code>, use it to\nparse input, and pass the result to <code>load</code>:</p>\n<div class=\"highlight js\"><pre class=\"editor editor-colors\"><div id=\"user-content--selector-context-root-\" class=\"deep-link\" href=\"#-selector-context-root-\" aria-hidden=\"true\" rel=\"nofollow\"><svg aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"deep-link-icon\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewbox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"><path d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path></svg></a>$( selector, [context], [root] )</h4>\n<p><code>selector</code> searches within the <code>context</code> scope which searches within the <code>root</code> scope. <code>selector</code> and <code>context</code> can be a string expression, DOM Element, array of DOM elements, or cheerio object. <code>root</code> is typically the HTML document string.</p>\n<p>This selector method is the starting point for traversing and manipulating the document. Like jQuery, it's the primary method for selecting elements in the document, but unlike jQuery it's built on top of the CSSSelect library, which implements most of the Sizzle selectors.</p>\n<div .not( function(index, elem) )</h4>\n<p>Remove elements from the set of matched elements. Given a jQuery object that represents a set of DOM elements, the <code>.not()</code> method constructs a new jQuery object from a subset of the matching elements. The supplied selector is tested against each element; the elements that don't match the selector will be included in the result. The <code>.not()</code> method can take a function as its argument in the same way that <code>.filter()</code> does. id=\"user-content-the-dom-node-object\" class=\"deep-link\" href=\"#the-dom-node-object\" aria-hidden=\"true\" rel=\"nofollow\"><svg aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"deep-link-icon\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewbox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"><path d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 6z\"></path></svg></a>The &quot;DOM Node&quot; object</h3>\n<p>Cheerio collections are made up of objects that bear some resemblence to <a href=\"https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/Node\" rel=\"nofollow\">browser-based DOM nodes</a>. You can expect them to define the following properties:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><code>tagName</code></li>\n<li><code>parentNode</code></li>\n<li><code>previousSibling</code></li>\n<li><code>nextSibling</code></li>\n<li><code>nodeValue</code></li>\n<li><code>firstChild</code></li>\n<li><code>childNodes</code></li>\n<li><code>lastChild</code></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><a id=\"user-content-screencasts\" class=\"deep-link\" href=\"#screencasts\" aria-hidden=\"true\" rel=\"nofollow\"><svg aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"deep-link-icon\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewbox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"><path d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path></svg></a>Screencasts</h2>\n<p><a href=\"http://vimeo.com/31950192\" rel=\"nofollow\">http://vimeo.com/31950192</a></p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>This video tutorial is a follow-up to Nettut's &quot;How to Scrape Web Pages with Node.js and jQuery&quot;, using cheerio instead of JSDOM + jQuery. This video shows how easy it is to use cheerio and how much faster cheerio is than JSDOM + jQuery.</p>\n</blockquote>\n<h2><a id=\"user-content-contributors\" class=\"deep-link\" A special thanks to:</p>\n<p><strong>• @FB55 for node-htmlparser2 &amp; CSSSelect:</strong>\nFelix has a knack for writing speedy parsing engines. He completely re-wrote both @tautologistic's <code>node-htmlparser</code> and @harry's <code>node-soupselect</code> from the ground up, making both of them much faster and more flexible. Cheerio would not be possible without his foundational work</p>\n<p><strong>• @jQuery team for jQuery:</strong>\nThe core API is the best of its class and despite dealing with all the browser inconsistencies the code base is extremely clean and easy to follow. Much of cheerio's implementation and documentation is from jQuery. Thanks guys.</p>\n<p><strong>• @visionmedia:</strong>\nThe style, the structure, the open-source&quot;-ness&quot; of this library comes from studying TJ's style and using many of his libraries. This dude consistently pumps out high-quality libraries and has always been more than willing to help or answer questions. You rock TJ.</p>\n<h2><a id=\"user-content-license\" class=\"deep-link\" href=\"#license\" aria-hidden=\"true\" rel=\"nofollow\"><svg aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"deep-link-icon\" height=\"16\"
